Implement the tooltip as an inline element (since no tooltip library exists)\n   - Render it as a small positioned div that closes on blur or touch end\n\nFor the implementation, I need to handle both mouse and touch events separately. On desktop, `onMouseDown` will start the timer while `onMouseUp` and `onMouseLeave` cancel it. On mobile, `onTouchStart` initiates the timer and `onTouchEnd` or `onTouchCancel` stops it. The tooltip appears near the button once the 300ms hold threshold is reached, then disappears when the user releases their input. I'll position it absolutely relative to the button's parent container.\n\nThe long-press behavior should work independently of other props—it always shows the tooltip with the line's full name, division, and express/local status, regardless of whether `onClick` is defined.\n\nSetting up the component... Writing the component JSX...\n\nActually, I'm realizing there's a potential issue with the disabled state—disabled buttons don't reliably fire mouse and touch events across different browsers, which would break the long-press detection. I need to reconsider whether disabling the button is the right approach here.\n\nLooking at the actual requirement, the tooltip should be available on long-press regardless of whether an onClick handler exists. So instead of disabling the button when there's no onClick, I should keep it enabled but style it to appear non-interactive, and let the long-press gesture work universally. I'm realizing the core issue: `disabled` blocks pointer events in Firefox, which prevents long-press from working even though we want it to. The backwards compatibility constraint means I need to keep the disabled appearance when there's no onClick, so wrapping the button in a span and attaching long-press handlers to the wrapper itself is the cleanest path forward—this preserves the button's disabled state for clicks while letting the wrapper capture touch events.
